  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5da7d0e1-60e1-4375-bcbd-394ff5b69cf4'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_56243770" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/56243770" />
    <a title="Sella Malin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/909992-sella-malin"><img alt="Sella Malin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277512197p2/909992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/56243770?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sella Malin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sella Malin" href="/user/show/909992-sella-malin">Sella Malin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer56243770&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56243770" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6440933084018645291">I knew it! I knew it all along! I knew that Leafpool and Crowfeather were Lionblaze's, Hollyleaf's, and Jayfeather's parents! I knew it from The Sight! And now it was finally revealed. YESSS!!! :)<br/><br/>I had NO CLUE about Hollyleaf being the one who killed Ashfur, though. I thought it was Squirrelflight for sure – there was SO much evidence! How could it be Hollyleaf? We're in her point of view all the time, in her head! How could we not know? Wouldn't she think about it before we find out from someon</span>
  <span id="freeText6440933084018645291" style="display:none">I knew it! I knew it all along! I knew that Leafpool and Crowfeather were Lionblaze's, Hollyleaf's, and Jayfeather's parents! I knew it from The Sight! And now it was finally revealed. YESSS!!! :)<br /><br />I had NO CLUE about Hollyleaf being the one who killed Ashfur, though. I thought it was Squirrelflight for sure – there was SO much evidence! How could it be Hollyleaf? We're in her point of view all the time, in her head! How could we not know? Wouldn't she think about it before we find out from someone else? It doesn't make sense. But, I mean, come on! Hollyleaf? HOLLYLEAF, the one who is always so dedicated to the warrior code? Kill someone? That's SO messed up! What's gotten into her?<br /><br />Okay, I seriously, actually think that Holly has literally gone mentally insane. First she kills Ashfur, then she lets everyone at the gathering know about Leafpool's secret (which is what she wanted to stop Ashfur from doing when she killed him! Dude! Wth?!?), then she kills HERSELF! She definitely lost her mind. It's kind of a shame – she used to be so sweet, and have so much potential!<br /><br />I can't believe she's not one of the Three of the prophecy anymore. It's like...all along I've thought I was standing on a carpet, and suddenly that carpet isn't there anymore – pulled out from under my feet – and I'm left tumbling to the ground. I just can't believe Hollyleaf is actually dead.<br /><br />That brings me to another thing. Hollyleaf's death was so...abrupt. I couldn't quite register or realize it had just happened, even after I finished the last page of the book. It's like...one moment she's screaming at her littermates, the next moment the tunnel has collapsed on top of her, and the book ends. It doesn't feel...real.<br /><br />It's kind of weird, because when she dies, neither Lion nor Jay are sad, or grieving, or anguished, or even a tiny bit distraught! They're just sort of like, “oh.” And then, “now the prophecy won't work. Too bad.” I mean, WHAT?!? Their sister just DIED! Even if she's a raving lunatic, she's still your sister! You should feel SOME grief that she died! It's not realistic.<br /><br />And no one else feels any grief, either. They're all just like, “oh well, whatever.” Even Leafpool doesn't show any pain! I mean, WHAT?!? I don't get it!<br /><br />I think Hollyleaf's death would actually feel real, and wouldn't be so hard to register, if someone actually had a reaction to it, instead of everyone just being indifferent. Whenever a cat dies, other cats are always shocked, or grieving, or something. But this time, no one even showed any emotion! It's so stupid and unrealistic! That part wasn't written well at all. I still feel like Hollyleaf's not really dead, or something.<br /><br />OMG! It was SO sad how Honeyfern died! That was utterly cruel! Berrynose FINALLY likes her back, and they're talking about how they're going to become mates and have kits together - and then the next moment, Honeyfern is dying! It's not fair! And the thing that made me SO pissed is that Leafpool DID NOTHING!! Is she a medicine cat or ISN'T SHE?!?! Don't just STAND there while Honeyfern is dying!!! DO SOMETHING!!! But nooo. She just sat there and looked sad while Honeyfern died. OMG!!! I hated her then!!!<br /><br />And about Leafpool...what will she do now? Will she get banished from the Clan? How come Firestar hasn't done anything about it yet? Is she not going to be a medicine cat anymore? Where will she go? How come she came back to the ThunderClan camp after the gathering? Is she just going to be the medicine cat again? How is everyone letting her? Are they just going to forget about it? I'm confused!<br /><br />Anyway, past all my ranting...I think this is the best book out of all three series of Warriors. No other book is as intense, dramatic, or disturbing. It definitely wins.<br /><br />Except, for the first time...I'm not looking forward to the next book so much. It's weird. Usually I'm dying for the next one in this series, but now...I think the Erins kind of ruined it for me by making Hollyleaf die in such an unreal way. Plus, I think it's pointless to keep going with the series. EVERYTHING has already happened. Everything is kind of OVER now. More books are just going to drag it on and on until there won't be much plot left. I think the Warrior series has done all it can, and while it has been an amazing series and one of my favorites, I think it's time it was over. There's only so much you can pull it out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6440933084018645291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_46246478" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46246478" />
    <a title="Featherheart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/996494-featherheart"><img alt="Featherheart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246157624p2/996494.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46246478?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Featherheart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Featherheart" href="/user/show/996494-featherheart">Featherheart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer46246478&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46246478" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6983096381266385878"><b>This review contains MAJOR spoilers.</b><br/>The writing was excellent, the characters believable, but the plot? I was disappointed in this last installment of Power of Three, reasons listed below:<br/>1. What was the point of having Hollyleaf through all the rest of the books if she wasn't one of the three and was just going to die? It makes the whole series seem a little pointless. I think the Erins did it because she didn't have any special powers like Lionblaze and Jayfeather, but still.<br/>2. I like continui</span>
  <span id="freeText6983096381266385878" style="display:none"><b>This review contains MAJOR spoilers.</b><br />The writing was excellent, the characters believable, but the plot? I was disappointed in this last installment of Power of Three, reasons listed below:<br />1. What was the point of having Hollyleaf through all the rest of the books if she wasn't one of the three and was just going to die? It makes the whole series seem a little pointless. I think the Erins did it because she didn't have any special powers like Lionblaze and Jayfeather, but still.<br />2. I like continuity and patterns, and this book and in fact series failed at that in several ways, the first being that each series is supposed to be one chapter in the history of the Clans and once it is over it is only a story for the elders to tell and no longer really spoken of. Obviously that's not the case with this series and the next. The whole six books were about learning about their powers, the cats who lived before, and about their parentage. The next series will likely be about the new kit, teaching and helping her learn to be one of the three, and actually coming into their power, so two series combined make up the story of the Three.<br />3. Maybe it's just my preference, but it seems way more mystical and prophecy-fulfilling for the Three to come from the same litter. Jayfeather and Lionblaze will always be closer than Dovekit or Ivykit will be to either of them. It kind of feels like the Erins made up a subsitute. I mean, why them and not Hollyleaf or whichever kit isn't chosen? The way we all thought it was made more sense.<br />4. Again on continuity, for the whole first two series and most of this one, halfClan, kittypet, and loner cats were distrusted, but eventually accepted. Why does Hollyleaf go on such a rampage to learn that she's among the long list? She already has kittypet blood in her. Surely being loyal is more important than parentage, and didn't she say something of that sort? It was pretty much like finding out you're adopted. You don't see adopted kids, at least I don't, trying to kill their real mother, failing to forgive real and adopted mothers, and trying to leave their home because of it.<br />5. This is just a minor note, but I didn't think the title made sense, this one or the last. The Sight refers to Jaypaw's sight, Dark River obviously the river, Outcast Stormfur and Brook's being outcast, and Eclipse the eclipse. All real things. But Long Shadows just seems to mean that the truth is hidden, and Sunrise that they are finally ready to begin using their power.<br />6. They knew what Sol could do, so why did they still help him escape and trust him? That seems like not learning one's lesson to me.<br />7. Finally, I was annoyed about all of Hollyleaf's previously mentioned actions at the end. I couldn't like her, and she is or was one of the protagonists.<br />To sum it up, if you don't analyze stories and just enjoy them, you'll love this book just as much as all the rest. But if you like continuity and things making sense like me, you'll be annoyed by this book. Either way, it's worth reading for the end of the story and the wonderful style of writing, just not as good as the rest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6983096381266385878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13759378094572073126" style="display:none">EPIC!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! Yeah this book is a close second to Long Shadows... The prologue is very well written and intriguing indeed! This book is almost as eventful as the last and is very hard to put down as it is like a mystery novel. Thunderclan get really determined to find out who killed ****** and a group of cats travel to the Sundrown place to hunt down sol and to get answers. This book keeps you guessing and is very interesting. When you find out the answer to a big question it was for me a total unexpected surprise but when you think about it, it makes sense. Jayfether becomes a bit of a detective himself as he searched for different answers (being the most curious of the three).A certain cat does certain (jaw-dropping) things at the ending of the book and I end up really disliking this cat. This cat is drove to near insanity and does major things that put her clan at risk. A suspenseful and emotional ending that is is sure to satisfy and surprise.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4320235290773352096">HMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM<br/><br/>Sunrise, as what i initially believed to be the conclusion of the power of three, their arc, the meaning of everything that has been raised etc. Not really sure if it's a spoiler to say that that's very wrong, and the story of the prophecy is still far, far from over.<br/><br/>There is a famous death in the fan community that occured in this book, something which I was aware of before I even began this series. And maybe I built it up too much, but my goodness was it a rushed death!!! I</span>
  <span id="freeText4320235290773352096" style="display:none">HMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM<br /><br />Sunrise, as what i initially believed to be the conclusion of the power of three, their arc, the meaning of everything that has been raised etc. Not really sure if it's a spoiler to say that that's very wrong, and the story of the prophecy is still far, far from over.<br /><br />There is a famous death in the fan community that occured in this book, something which I was aware of before I even began this series. And maybe I built it up too much, but my goodness was it a rushed death!!! It happened in the blink of an eye and felt absolutely pointless, like the Erins had no way of fixing the problems Hollyleaf was suffering from so they felt they had no choice but to just... kill her? Or was it the other way around - because she 'needs to die' for the sake of the plot, as we all know, was it that they struggled to find a believable way to kill her off and failed anyway? Make it make sense!<br /><br />So unfortunately that really chipped a whole star off of a volume that I really thought was going to be explosive. And it was! In many ways - but this unfortunately was a shame. What kept the rating up for me was that I really, genuinely believe that Squirrelflight killed Ashfur - the fact that the Erins managed to make Hollyleaf do this off screen and then make her life continue as kind of normal and re-focus all her worried energy into something the reader interprets as negative feelings aimed at Squirrelflight was so fucking clever and the plot twist of the century. I really don't know what I missed, and I'm so impressed! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4320235290773352096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_184281665" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184281665" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5222564-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302651637p2/5222564.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184281665?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/5222564-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5222564-scott?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer184281665&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184281665" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9765489409474085725">Please be sure that you have read the book before reading this review. I don't want to spoil anything for you in the following reflection ...<br/><br/>I found this installation of the continuing saga of our ThunderClan heroes to be a fitting end to the six books in the "Power of Three" series. I entered this book with a number of BURNING questions ... one about parental obligations and one about who had committed a crime that was completely against the Warrior code. I rd this book with growing anticipatio</span>
  <span id="freeText9765489409474085725" style="display:none">Please be sure that you have read the book before reading this review. I don't want to spoil anything for you in the following reflection ...<br /><br />I found this installation of the continuing saga of our ThunderClan heroes to be a fitting end to the six books in the "Power of Three" series. I entered this book with a number of BURNING questions ... one about parental obligations and one about who had committed a crime that was completely against the Warrior code. I rd this book with growing anticipation as I had definitely formed my own opinions about who was responsible in each case ... and I felt a sense of triumph as my first prediction was confirmed ... followed by an incredible sense of shock as my second prediction wasn't even in the ballpark. All of this was revealed swiftly as one of the answers confronted the other about the first but was instead confronted indirectly about the second. Hopefully, that only makes sense to those who have read this book.<br /><br />The cliffhanger at the end of the book promises that the next series (Omen of the Stars) will continue on ... the questions that I entered "Sunrise" with have been answered. However, as with all great stories, the finding of answers often leads to more and deeper questions. Of these deeper questions, I now have many ...<br /><br />Along those same lines, there also were a number of very surprising turns in this book that had me asking "Why?" often and repeatedly. I was surprised that following his dreams with StarClan that Jayfeather would allow his clamnates, including his brother and sister, to travel the along the dangerous journey to the Sun Drowned Place in search of Midnight and Sol. There is also much inner-turmoil presented very tactfully by the authors as the hidden secrets weave their poison through Squirrelflight's trio of kits. Hollyleaf, Lionblaze, and Jayfeather often say and do one thing while we, the readers, are privileged to also hear what they are truly thinking. Chief among these from my perspective would be Hollyleaf as her commitment and loyalty to the Warrior Code becomes painfully apparent as it skews her relationship with her family and the larger Thunderclan. As for the heinous crime committed against Ashfur, I didn't see that coming but enjoyed trying to piece together the clues and motivations in my personal investigation of the crime ... I thought I had it solved but was sorely mistaken. The snake attack ... why? Honeyfern ... why? Revelation of secrets at the Gathering ... why? Tunnels collapsing ... why? Refusal to speak with or listen to mother and aunt ... WHY??? As I said, so many deep questions!<br /><br />Of any cats, the three cats identified by the prophesy certainly realize that the truth can't be hidden ... yet they continue to try to maintain their own secrets ... it's just a continuing dichotomy that makes the reader hunger for more in the search for reasons ... and justifications ... and answers. <br /><br />I look forward to the release of the final two books in the "Omen of the Stars" series so that I can find more answers ... and ask more questions ...</span>
  <a data-text-id="9765489409474085725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2137525265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2137525265" />
    <a title="Matthew Aker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71915679-matthew-aker"><img alt="Matthew Aker" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2137525265?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Aker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Aker" href="/user/show/71915679-matthew-aker">Matthew Aker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137525265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5013841198182698605">I loved the action and surprises in this book. This book definitely earned the title of the final book in the "Power of Three" series. <br/><br/>I loved how throughout the book Jayfeather continued to show how intelligent he is. I loved the moments when the prophecy truly began to unfold and the shocker at the end. I love to see how Erin Hunter was able to make a blind cat's perspective so interesting. Jayfeather is the perfect cat for the typical grouchy, smart, medicine cat that we have seen in almost e</span>
  <span id="freeText5013841198182698605" style="display:none">I loved the action and surprises in this book. This book definitely earned the title of the final book in the "Power of Three" series. <br /><br />I loved how throughout the book Jayfeather continued to show how intelligent he is. I loved the moments when the prophecy truly began to unfold and the shocker at the end. I love to see how Erin Hunter was able to make a blind cat's perspective so interesting. Jayfeather is the perfect cat for the typical grouchy, smart, medicine cat that we have seen in almost every medicine cat. I hope to see him in the next series being just as sarcastic and grouchy.<br /><br />It's great to see Loinblaze fighting to find out where he belongs. For some cats, they just keep on making the wrong choices and not even realizing it. I can tell that he will be a great cat to follow in the next series. I love his role in the prophecy. He has an ability that no cat has ever had before. He single-handedly could destroy the clans, or save them.<br /><br />This book is really sad when you see what happened to Hollyleaf throughout the book. I hated seeing her in her rages of confusion and anger. I hate the rage between her and her 'mom,' Squirrelflight. I have to admit though, I was intrigued to see a cat so full of emotions that I would think only a human could be able of feeling. Erin Hunter used Hollyleaf to show that she can write very sad endings. I hope that in the next series we get to see her, in her old loveable manner.<br /><br />One thing I love about Erin Hunter is she always is able to find trouble from almost anywhere. I love the way she has, once again, been able to not only have clan fighting, but she was able to have fighting involving the outsider, Sol. It was great to see such a persuasive cat cause so much trouble throughout the series. In some ways, you can apply Sol to real-world people. There are people in the world who are able to be very persuasive and get people to do what they want. The way the author can make people connect make-believe cat lives apply to the real world is incredible. <br /><br />It is a wonderful feeling seeing how Firestar has grown since the first series. He is my most favorite character, and I love how he was able to deal with the difficult situations he faced this series in the mature, leader-like way he is supposed to. I don't know what life he is on exactly, but I do know that when he dies it will be tragic for me. I have loved seeing him as the best leader of Thunderclan. <br /><br />Even though I loved this book, I wish that Erin Hunter had more fighting, like in the previous two series finales. I hope the next series is as interesting as this one, and I am looking forward to seeing it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5013841198182698605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13840515525808172470" style="display:none">	A terrible crime has been committed; a fellow Thunderclan cat has killed one of their own. The answer to this great mystery may surprise you. Meanwhile Jayfeather, Hollyleaf, and Lionblaze are closer then ever in finding out who their true parents really are. However, the truth is hidden behind a wall off lies that could lead to an unexpected death of one cat. Danger lurks behind every bush and tree, striking out unexpected ways, and the loyalty between family and the warrior code will be tested for one of the three. The outcome will change the lives of everyone for generations to come.<br /><br />The book warriors the power of three, sunrise was the most surprising and fast paced books I have ever read. It had a pace that’s equal to that of a jet slicing through the air. For example, a cat would be hunting one moment then be running for their life in another. Also I was stunned by the situation when Hollyleaf reveals a grave secret to the clans. This book answered many of my questions but not in the way I thought. Like my question of who the mysterious prophecy of “ there will be three, kin of your kin, who hold the power of the stars in their paws” mentions and what it means. This book has to be the best of the series and is worth reading a second time over.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText6128847901592881077" style="display:none">I am utterly confused about this book, im not sure whether i should give it 1 star or 5!<br /><br />First of all i dont think that Hollyleaf's death was very well written out, i mean one minute shes raving and shouting and the next minute Jayfeather and Lionblaze are like "Oh... shes dead, dangit now there's no prophecy" i mean c'mon show a little emotion here! All of the evidence pointed to it! <br /><br />Lastly, where will Leafpool go now? Will she become an outsider? Still part of the clan but not a medicine cat? I am interested to find out, but i was so so sad that Hollyleaf had to blab because i really liked Leafpool and Squirrelflight! Now they are overcome with grief and have lost all of the trust of their clanmates, friends, mates and kits trust and love!<br /><br />I am interested to see what will happen in the next book....</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Syed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Syed" href="/user/show/47882382-sarah-syed">Sarah Syed</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1889442022&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1889442022" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16118053029233892195">This book was ok but the authors could have written it better in some parts. I think the theme in this book is to stay determined. In Sunrise, Jayfeather wants to really know who his parents are. So he has to go through tough conditions, only for the mission to get harder. But he's determined to continue and find the origin to his past. Hollyleaf died in this book, but on the other hand, the authors poorly interpreted her death. Hollyleaf's storyline changed rapidly and she went from nice to cru</span>
  <span id="freeText16118053029233892195" style="display:none">This book was ok but the authors could have written it better in some parts. I think the theme in this book is to stay determined. In Sunrise, Jayfeather wants to really know who his parents are. So he has to go through tough conditions, only for the mission to get harder. But he's determined to continue and find the origin to his past. Hollyleaf died in this book, but on the other hand, the authors poorly interpreted her death. Hollyleaf's storyline changed rapidly and she went from nice to cruel, she even went as far to kill Ashfur because he knew a secret between the 2 of them. And then Hollyleaf dies. Her death is so bland and visionless. It feels as if Hollyleaf's not actually dead, and the authors want the readers to think that she is dead. It wasn't the best book from Warriors, and this is the last book in the Power of Three series until the fourth series Omen From The Stars. And I believe that The Fourth Apprentice (the first book in the Omen of The Stars) has more potential then Sunrise did. It feels like the Hunter's just threw in some action and deaths into this book without piecing it together. I rate this book 2 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16118053029233892195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3050080839" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3050080839" />
    <a title="Historyprincess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess"><img alt="Historyprincess" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3050080839?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Historyprincess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Historyprincess" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess">Historyprincess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30458279-sunrise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12881308-historyprincess?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3050080839&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3050080839" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15483731829384585216">Premise: A great ThunderClan warrior has been murdered, and only Lionblaze, Hollyleaf, and Jayfeather know why. Now that the shocking lie they'd believed all their lives has been revealed to them, they're determined to track down the killer and discover their true lineage. But the more the three siblings find out, the more they realize just how devastating the truth about their origins has the potential to be – not only for themselves, but for all of ThunderClan. The one thing that's certain is </span>
  <span id="freeText15483731829384585216" style="display:none">Premise: A great ThunderClan warrior has been murdered, and only Lionblaze, Hollyleaf, and Jayfeather know why. Now that the shocking lie they'd believed all their lives has been revealed to them, they're determined to track down the killer and discover their true lineage. But the more the three siblings find out, the more they realize just how devastating the truth about their origins has the potential to be – not only for themselves, but for all of ThunderClan. The one thing that's certain is that their understanding of the prophecy is about to change forever.<br /><br />Story/Writing: Man…wow…I…I am just completely and utterly speechless. This story so completely and utterly floored me emotionally that it's gonna be hard for me to review this one, only because at this point I'm grasping for straws in terms of what words I can use to describe how much of an impact this brilliant book had on me. On the one hand, I feel like this is one of those books where, no matter how I feel about it, I'm gonna make someone mad. I'm guessing this book is a bit of a controversial one in the fandom, like it's one of those books that you really do either love or hate. But I digress. This is my honest opinion, and I'm gonna give it. While I think all the books so far have been great, every now and then I come across ones that are especially great. And this one is definitely one of the especially great ones! If you thought things were dramatic in the previous arc, by the time this arc ends, the drama level gets dialed up to eleven! Pretty much everything that happens in this book – come to think of it, pretty much everything that happens in this entire arc – builds up to a dramatic climax that just got me right in the gut of my feels! I believe that an ending, whether good or bad, must be earned. And this one feels so earned it's just unbelievable! It got so many strong emotions out of me that did feel awful. Yet at the same time, in a bizarre way, I got excited that I was feeling these strong yet awful emotions! I was feeling what the authors wanted me to feel and I knew it! That was what got me all pumped up! And given that this book ends on a cliffhanger and leads into the arc I have been waiting to read for MONTHS, it added a whole new dimension of excitement for me! I'm writing this in the middle of the night and I don't know if I'm gonna be able to sleep! It was that great! Not to mention, the title was perfect too! Not only because the book ends at that time of day, but also because light has finally been shed on where the three siblings came from, and this arc ends with the dawning of a new one!<br /><br />Characters: Wow, do the characters in this book just blow my mind with how they're written! I know that certain things that certain characters do in this book won't be universally loved, nor are they really meant to be. And I myself definitely don't agree with every single action from every single character. But from a storytelling perspective, I ate all this character development up like candy! The three siblings in particular develop such a strong bond that it made me wish I had something like that with my own two siblings. That all said, there's plenty to like about them as individuals also. Although, again, I say that with a storytelling perspective in mind.<br /><br />Hollyleaf – I think it's fitting that Hollyleaf is on the cover, given that she's the main catalyst in causing the epically dramatic climax and is assumed dead by the end. Moving on, I've said before in previous reviews that she's the character I most strongly identify with in this series so far. But man, that has never been more true than in this book! I can't help but wonder if the authors on the Erin Hunter team spied on me and wrote Hollyleaf's character around me. That's how surreal it felt for me as I read about her in this book. With the exception of her killing Ashfur, I felt like I was reading about myself in this world I've come to love so much! Speaking of which though, when it was revealed that Hollyleaf killed Ashfur…I…I was shocked. That was… Wow. Reading that was so hard for me and made me feel like someone whacked me across the face. I can't remember ever feeling like that about a character in a book, or at least not this strongly. I wanted so badly for it to not be true, but by the time Jayfeather looked into her memories, I was forced to face the facts. And speaking of that, whether or not you agree with Hollyleaf revealing everything in front of all the Clans, and even if she did participate in the search for Sol to keep her own Clan's focus somewhere else, you gotta admit her utter commitment to the truth in the end is commendable. While I don't completely condone her actions, I totally understand where she's coming from. As far as she's concerned, her entire life has been a lie. Not only was she lied to about her lineage, at least in part. She came from a twice over forbidden union between a medicine cat and a cat from another Clan. Her faith in the warrior code has been obliterated. And she's not even the third one in the prophecy. By the end of the book, I felt the tremendous amount of pain and anger and complete and utter devastation she fell into. Some may disagree with me on this, but on the one hand, I was glad she revealed everything. I wouldn't want to live a lie for the rest of my life. And the Clans deserve to know when the warrior code has been broken this severely. On the other hand though, it was tragic to read about her descent into this level of low, to the point where she was not only willing to publicly humiliate her own mother, but ready to outright kill her as well. And now that her brothers think she's dead… Geez, that was all just hardcore!<br /><br />Jayfeather – I like that the authors, for a time, separated Hollyleaf and Lionblaze from Jayfeather. It reminded me of "Dawn," where we switch between the points of view of Squirrelflight and Leafpool (then Squirrelpaw and Leafpaw). Anyway, the closer he got to finding out who their real parents are, the more bizarrely anxious I got. I was also wondering how much more blind (no pun intended) he could get when the answer was right in front of him. But in the end, it made sense. I knew it was gonna be a monumental reveal. But I wasn't expecting how heavily it was going to weigh on him in particular. The one who mentored him also gave birth to him. And then he could only watch (so to speak) as his sister revealed everything to all the Clans at the Gathering. Yet still, on top of that, he believes his sister is now dead. Man, for all the times he can be a grump, I seriously felt for Jayfeather in this book! Sometimes, I even wanted him to go back to his dry, sarcastic self. At the same time though, this is probably the best that Jayfeather has been so far in the series (at least, for me). I thought he was so sweet when he helped Whitewing deliver her kits, and I loved how excited he got when he realized one of them could be the third one in the prophecy. Even so, I deeply felt the anguish he went through when he tried to reason with his sister, only to lose her to the tunnels. It shows that, while he's not the most affectionate cat, he deeply loves his siblings and would go to any lengths to help him. And now he's got to deal with being ThunderClan's only medicine cat now that Leafpool has resigned. All I can say is, I wish him the very best!<br /><br />Lionblaze – While I never really bonded with Lionblaze as much as I did with Hollyleaf and Jayfeather, I can say with complete and utter confidence that, just as the case was with his brother, the way Lionblaze is portrayed here is the best so far in the series. And just like it was for his brother and sister, the revelation of his true lineage impacted him in a unique way as well. On the one hand, it should be a relief that he's in fact not related to Tigerstar and Hawkfrost like he originally thought. But that also means he's not related to Brambleclaw, who is arguably the noblest cat in all the Clans. Plus, not only did he have a brief fling with a cat from his father's Clan. Lionblaze now knows that he himself is half-Clan, and most of his life has been a struggle to make sure his utmost loyalty is to ThunderClan. Not to mention, even though his own mentor was ready to let him and his siblings die, his mentor still died a violent death. And then, it turns out the one who killed Ashfur is his own sister, who now might be dead herself… I'm kinda surprised he didn't go as south as Hollyleaf did. He has almost as much stuff weighing on him as her, and his brother. Then again, he also participated in the search for Sol yet ended up being willing to show him the way to escape. Yeah, turns out Sol was innocent, but it's the principle. And yet even then, as bold and impulsive as Lionblaze can be, even he probably wouldn't be so daring as Hollyleaf to reveal everything about their secret at a Gathering of all places. All I can say is I hope he can prove his loyalty to ThunderClan, and perhaps even train Dovekit, given how much experience he has while still needing to learn some responsibility.<br /><br />Leafpool – Wow… Leafpool, as much as I like you, I hate to say it, but you screwed up big time! In all seriousness though, Leafpool will always be one of my favorite characters, and yet, I couldn't entirely blame Hollyleaf for revealing what her mother had done at the Gathering. Even if her children did end up being two of the three cats in the prophecy, she still broke the warrior code severely. Worse, she tried to cover it up. I say this not out of spite but out of a sense of sadness. I still do really like Leafpool, and I'm sorry she had to pay in such a humiliating and awful way. Just as she told Hollyleaf, she had to give her kits away and could never claim them as her own; she had to convince her sister to lie to everyone, including her own mate, who's the deputy of ThunderClan; she was publicly shunned by the cat she once loved; she had to own up to what she did in front of her fellow medicine cats, her family, and all of the Clans, not just her own; she's broken the warrior code in such an unprecedented way; she was forced to resign from being a medicine cat; she was exposed by her own daughter, who told her she hated her and wanted her to die; and now, that same daughter could be lost to her forever in every way. I don't think I've seen a cat in this series suffer this much since Mapleshade or even Yellowfang. If anything, it makes for a good morality tale, in that it teaches the reader that there are consequences for their actions, even if those consequences get delayed for a long time. As awful as I think things went for her, though, I am glad that she did own up to what she did and resigned from being a medicine cat, however hard it must've been for her.<br /><br />Various Other Characters – Oh Sol, you sneaky, conniving son of a… Well, whatever. You all know what I mean! While I know Sol doesn't have much of a soul (pun intended) despite all his charm and charisma, it is bizarrely fascinating that he still ate up every page he was on. Even when Midnight said he wasn't the killer, he had this mysterious sense of "Is he or isn't he?" about him. That said, he also showed how much of a hypocrite he is, telling cats that they can live however they want, just so long as they live how he wants. Not to mention he tries to get into a power play with the siblings and them tells them to grab power in a way almost identical to how Tigerstar grabbed for it. I also thought Jingo and her street cats were pretty cool, and their story about how Sol appeared to make things better but ended up making them far worse was pretty tough to read. I'm glad that Flamepaw did get to be Littlecloud's apprentice after all! Purdy appears again, and while he certainly provides some levity when it's needed, the authors gave him a surprising amount of depth, too. He's a lonely old cat with nowhere to go now that his human owner is dead. It's no wonder he so passionately defends Sol. I don't know whether or not he'll stay permanently in ThunderClan, but at this point in his life, I wouldn't be surprised if he does. Out of all the cats that participated in the patrol to find Sol, I was oddly enough rooting for Birchfall, 'cause I knew he had a mate expecting kits at home, and I also know those kits would be Dovekit and Ivykit. Not to mention the way he acts when he sees them for the first time is so adorable! Speaking of which, wow, Crowfeather, you've lost a ton of my respect. Even if you want to stay loyal to your own Clan and have nothing to do with Leafpool anymore, the very least you could've done was own up to the fact that this whole thing was arguably just as much your fault as it was hers! I seriously hope your super edition redeems you to me somehow. I also felt terribly sorry for Brambleclaw when he found out that his mate lied to him and that the kits he'd been proud of his whole life were not his at all. And StarClan knows how well Firestar is gonna deal with the revelation that both his daughters had broken the warrior code and lied to him. Speaking of StarClan, I hope you find peace there Honeyfern! Even if you were an airhead at times, you gave your life to save Briarkit's when the snake attacked. And for that, you'll always have my respect.<br /><br />Overall: This was a very emotional and heavy book to read, but I found it all worth it! I know some things that happened here won't be popular with everyone, but I thoroughly enjoyed it all from a storytelling viewpoint. If you're willing to read with that perspective, check this one out! Or, more preferably, read all the others in the rest of the arc before this. This one is the last one in the "Power of Three" arc, after all, and it gave me an emotionally explosive ending to its own story and the arc as a whole!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15483731829384585216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Th4XlnUcOfpRkWGIWUoSdAHb/kjhRMPEeMDwaw/Lshg44R6GoQRCMDOHFzYic+aMpUZWT7yBfh+lqQcMq+yJcg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

As well as having a great respect for nature in all its forms, Erin enjoys creating rich mythical explanations for animal behavior, shaped by her interest in astronomy and standing stones.</span>
